## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics) — nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear second-order oscillators. Typical physics includes nonlinear restoring forces, damping (linear/nonlinear), and external/parametric forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -(c0 * x) (small oscillations about stable equilibrium)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper model in state-space form)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (nonlinear stiffness + viscous losses)
- Sinusoidally forced oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic external drive)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical nonlinear forced resonance/chaos model)
- Pendulum-type restoring force: dv_dt = -(c0 * sin(c1 * x)) - c2 * v (large-angle restoring torque with damping)
- Parametric (Mathieu-type) stiffness modulation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness/parametric resonance)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag-like dissipation at higher speeds)
- Cubic velocity damping: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (nonlinear dissipation in some mechanical/electrical analogs)
- Van der Pol-type self-excitation: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small amplitude, limit-cycle oscillations)
- Potential-derived force (general polynomial potential): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (higher-order stiffness from a symmetric potential expansion)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force symmetry: for symmetric potentials, dv_dt is typically an odd function of x (e.g., x, x**3, sin(c*x)), implying left-right symmetric motion.
- Damping sign constraint: dissipative terms are typically odd in v and oppose motion (e.g., -c*v, -c*v*Abs(v), -c*v**3), ensuring energy decreases when unforced.
- Nonlinear stiffness identification: appearance of x**3 (or higher odd powers) indicates hardening/softening behavior and amplitude-dependent frequency.
- Self-excited oscillations: factors like (c0 - x**2) * v indicate amplitude-dependent (possibly negative) damping leading to stable limit cycles (van der Pol family).
- External forcing signature: explicit dependence on t via sin/cos terms suggests driven response, resonance peaks, and potentially quasiperiodic/chaotic regimes when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric excitation signature: time dependence multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) points to Mathieu-type instability tongues and parametric resonance.
- Dry friction / Coulomb-like effects: terms proportional to -c*sign(v) (often modeled via -c*v/(Abs(v)+c1)) create stick-slip and non-smooth dynamics.
- Non-smooth restoring elements: terms like -c*Abs(x) or -c*x*Abs(x) can model impacts/backlash/piecewise stiffness, often producing harmonics and sharp transitions.

-2.5126990598325\,x^3\;-\;2.5126990598325\,x(0.0921849151045819\,t+1)\;-\;0.774919680656294\,\sin(v)
\]
So GT contains exactly:
- an \(x^3\) term with coefficient \(-2.5126990598325\)
- an \(x t\) term with coefficient \(-2.5126990598325\cdot 0.0921849151045819\) (linear in \(t\), not exponential, not sinusoidal)
- an \(x\) term with coefficient \(-2.5126990598325\)
- a \(\sin(v)\) term with coefficient \(-0.774919680656294\)
- **no** plain \(v\), \(v^3\), \(v|v|\), \(x|x|\), \(x^5\), etc.
- **no** \(\log(\cdot)\), \(\exp(\cdot)\), \(\cos(\cdot)\) dependence.

Now check candidates (constants in candidates are free, but functional forms must be able to reduce to GT).

1) Has \(c7\,x\sin(c8 t+c9)\) (sinusoidal in \(t\)), and \(\log(\cdot)\) in \(v\). GT needs linear-in-\(t\) multiplying \(x\) and a pure \(\sin(v)\) term (not inside log). Cannot convert \(\sin(\text{affine }t)\) into \((a t+b)\) for all \(t\). No match.

2) Has \(c7 x e^{c8 t}\) (exponential in \(t\)) and \(\log(\cdot)\) in \(v\). Cannot become \(x(\gamma t+1)\) for all \(t\). No match.

3) Has \(x\sin(c6 t+c7)\) (sinusoidal in \(t\)), plus absolute-value nonlinearities \(v|v|\), \(x|x|\), and rational \(v/(c9+|v|)\). GT has none of these and needs \(\sin(v)\). No match.

4) Similar issue: \(x\sin(\cdot)\), plus \(x^5\), \(v|v|\), rational in \(|v|\). No match.

5) Has \(x e^{c5 t}\), \(x^5,x^7\), \(v^3\), rational in \(|v|\). GT needs linear \(t\) and \(\sin(v)\). No match.

6) Has exponentials in \(t\), \(\cos(c8 x)\), \(v^3\), \(v|v|\). No match.

7) Has \(x\sin(\cdot)\) in \(t\), \(x|x|\), \(v^3\), \(v|v||x|\). No match.

8) Has \(x\sin(\cdot)\), \(x^5,x^7\), \(v^3\), \(v|v|\). No match.

9) Has \(x|x|\), \(x\sin(\cdot)\), \(v|v|\), \(v^3\). No match.

10) Has \(x\sin(\cdot)\), \(v^3\), \(v|v|\). No match.

11) Has \(x|x|\), \(x\sin(\cdot)\), \(v^3\), \(v|v|\). No match.

12) Has \(x\sin(\cdot)\) and \(x\cos(\cdot)\) time-periodic terms; GT needs \(x(\gamma t+1)\). No match.

14) Has \(x e^{c5 t}\) and \(v\sin(c8 t+c9)\) (time-dependent forcing in \(v\)), plus \(v^3\). GT has \(\sin(v)\) (argument \(v\), not \(t\)). No match.

- None contains a plain \(\sin(v)\) term outside of log or time dependence; only candidates 1–2 have a sine of \(v\) but it is inside \(\log(1+c4\sin(\cdot))\), which cannot equal a linear multiple of \(\sin(v)\) for all \(v\) (unless coefficient of log is 0, which removes it entirely).
- None can produce the required \(x(\gamma t+1)\) factor (linear in \(t\)) because their \(t\)-dependence is via \(\sin(\cdot)\), \(\cos(\cdot)\), or \(e^{(\cdot)t}\), not an affine function of \(t\).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO11)
============================================================
GT: -beta*sin(v) - omega0**c0*(gamma*t + c1)*x - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-2.5126990598325*x**3 - 2.5126990598325*x*(0.0921849151045819*t + 1) - 0.774919680656294*sin(v)`

Expanding: `-2.5126990598325*x**3 - 2.5126990598325*x - 0.231690668498698*x*t - 0.774919680656294*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `x**3` (cubic)
3. `x*t` (linear in x times t)
4. `sin(v)` (sine of v)

Now I need to check if each candidate can reproduce these exact basis functions.

**Key observations:**
- The GT requires `sin(v)` — candidates using `v`, `v**3`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v/(c+Abs(v))`, `log(...)` etc. cannot exactly reproduce `sin(v)`.
- The GT requires `x*t` — candidates need a term proportional to `x*t`.

Let me check which candidates have both `sin(v)` and `x*t` (or equivalent):

**`x*t` equivalents:** 
- `x*sin(c*t + c)` cannot produce `x*t` (sin is periodic, t is not)
- `x*exp(c*t)` cannot produce `x*t` (exponential ≠ linear)
- `x*cos(c*t)` cannot produce `x*t`

None of the candidates contain an explicit `x*t` term. So I need to check if any combination of terms can produce `x*t`.

**`sin(v)` check:**
- Most candidates use `v`, `v**3`, `v*Abs(v)`, etc. — these are polynomial/piecewise, NOT `sin(v)`.
- Candidates 1, 2 have `log(c*sin(c+c*v)+1)` — this is NOT `sin(v)`.
- No candidate contains a bare `sin(v)` term.

Since `sin(v)` is a transcendental function that cannot be represented by polynomials in `v` (like `v`, `v**3`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v/(c+|v|)`), and `x*t` (a product of two independent variables) cannot be represented by `x*exp(c*t)`, `x*sin(c*t+c)`, or `x*cos(c*t)`, **none of the candidates can match the GT**.

Let me verify this systematically for all 50 candidates:

- **Candidates 1-2:** Have `log(c*sin(v)+1)` — not `sin(v)`. NO MATCH.
- **Candidates 3-13:** Use `v`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v**3`, `v/(c+|v|)` for v-dependence, and `x*sin(c*t+c)` or `x*cos(c*t)` for t-dependence. Neither can produce `sin(v)` or `x*t`. NO MATCH.
- **Candidates 14-50:** Use `v`, `v**3` for v-dependence (can't produce `sin(v)`), and `x*exp(c*t)`, `x*cos(c*t)`, `exp(c*t)*sin(c*x+c)`, etc. for t-dependence (can't produce `x*t`). NO MATCH.
